exchangers and miscellaneous equipment; and
(e)   Auxiliary Facilities, comprising administration building, utility services.
Daian Wastewater Collection, Treatment and Disposal
26.         The major water pollution issues in Dalian relate to the need for protection
of coastal water quality, principally in terms of recreational waters and aquaculture. A
total of eight wastewater treatment and disposal schemes have been identified in Dalian for
completion by the year 2020 to deal with projected municipal and industrial wastewater
flows of about 640,000 m3/d at that time. The plants have been prioritized, in part in
terms of size, to ensure maximum environmental impact by dealing with the largest flows



- 72 -                        ANHUI3
first. The plants at Malan and Chunliu, with estimated flows in 2020 of 190,000 and
100,000 m3ld account for the major pollution loads, are given first priority. To date, only
the Chunliu plant has been constructed.
27.         The existing Chunliu plant, commissioned in 1988, was designed to treat a
flow of 60,000 m3/d, but is presently operating at about 25 percent of its rated capacity due
primarily to deficiencies in the sewerage system. Sewerage system improvements would
be undertaken to divert additional wastewater flows to the Chunliu wastewater treatment
plant, and the plant would be refurbished to enhance treatment efficiency and to realize its
original design capacity. A new wastewater treatment facility would be provided at Malan
River with a capacity of 120,000 m3/d, with the objective of improving water quality in
recreational waters and aquaculture areas of the adjacent Heishijiao Bay. Sludge from both
plants would be disposed of at the Maoyingzi landfill site.
28.         Due to water supply constraints in Dalian and the high cost of future water
source developments, reuse of treated effluent by industrial units is an important
consideration. Both the Chunliu (after upgrading) and the Malan River plants would
provide teriary treatment for significant proportions of the treated wastewater for industrial
reuse.
29.         Proposed Component ($60.0 million). The works proposed under this
component are as follows:
Chunliu System

reinforced concrete or other pipe materials in sizes from about 400 mm to

upgrading, control system, sludge drying/removal with capacity about
60,000 m3/d;
(d) Tertiary Treatment and Wastewater Recovery comprising sand filtration
and chlorination for a flow of 40,000 m3/d, pumping station and distribution
mains;
Malan System
(e)   Municipal Interceptor Sewer totaling about 3.5 km of reinforced concrete
or other pipe materials in sizes from about 500 mm to 1,200 mm diameter;

Dalian Municipal Solid Waste Management
31.         The objectives of this component are to alleviate the environmental pollution
and health risks associated with the present solid waste management system in DaLian, to
provide a better collection service, to enhance the reliability and operational efficiency of
the transportation system, and to provide for environmentally sound disposal of the waste
collected from domestic, industrial and commercial sources.
32.         A self-managed and self-financed, autonomious company, the Dalian Solid
Waste Company, has been established to be responsible for operation of the transfer
station, the transportation system and the landfill. The necessary company charters have
been written. A tariff structure for the transfer-transport services, as well as disposal
chnarges, have been adopted. The Dalian Municipal Government has issued the necessary
operating licenses to the new company, and the rate structure has been approved, but
would not be put into effect until the transfer station and the transportation system have
been installed.
33.        The administrative municipal districts (Zhang Shan, Xi Gang, Sha Hekou
and Gan Jing Zi) and the Dalian Construction Bureau, under the Dalian Municipal
Government, would continue to be responsible for providing solid waste collection
services, street sweeping, cleansing of public areas, and for special services on request
from industry and commerce.
34.        Industry, commerce and institutional entities would be responsible for
collection and transportation of their own waste.
35.         The solid waste management component comprises of:
(a)   Replacing the existing 99 open collection trucks and open public waste bins
with 56 sealed collection trucks (5-ton) equipped for mechanical loading of
bins with lids. This would not only reduce the number of vehicles in



- 75 -                        ANNEX-3
operation, but would make collection more cost-efficient, reduce littering of
the streets, and eliminate the present open public containers, which are
eyesores and a source of bad odor in an otherwise clean city;
(b)   Replacing the existing open and uncontrolled transfer site at Sl-ouyu Bay,
about 10 km from the city center, and the present open dumper trucks used
to transport the waste the 33 km to the Maoyingzi landfill, with a modemn,
enclosed, transfer station with capacity to handle up to 1,500 tons per day,
and provides one-day temporary storage. The waste would be transported
to the landfill in 20-ton containers hauled by 15 large semitrailers. The
about 120,000 rn3 of waste that currently remain at this site would be
removed and transported to the landfill.  This would eliminate an
uncontrolled source of pollution of the Shouyu Bay, greatly improve the
visual impression of this important industrial development area, reduce air
pollution from open fires and bad odor from the decomposing waste. The
transportation would be more effective, and there would be less traffic from
the larger-capacity vehicles;
(c)   Upgrading the present waste dump at Maoyingzi, on the shoreline of the
Bohai Bay to a sanitary landfill standard, which would be able to handle
about 2,550 tons per day. The selected site has capacity for about 20 years
of filling. A leachate system would be developed that minimizes seepage
into the groundwater and the bay, the landfill gas system would consist of
extraction wells and collector pipes, blowers and burners. Provision would
be made for gas utilization to be introduced at a later stage. Plant and
equipment for waste movement and compaction, cover material handling and
support functions would be provided. The site would also have office
facilities, scales, and truck/container washing bays; and
(d)   A separate institutional development and training project aimed at enabling
the Dalian Solid Waste Company staff to operate and manage the transfer
station, transportation and sanitary landfill efficiently and cost effectively is
included.

Jlnzou Water Supply
37.        The present water supply for Jinzhou is derived entirely from groundwater
abstracted close to the city mainly from a shallow aquifer recharged by the Xiaoling and
Nuer Rivers, and is unable to support significant increases in demand. In addition, four
of the seven groundwater sources :.re at risk of contamination resulting from inadequate
wastewater management.
38.         Groundwater assessment indioated that significant additional groundwater
resources yielding up to 300,000 m3/d are avb-. ible in the Daling-Xiaoling alluvial fan area
to the east of the city. Detailed studies confiimed the availability of at least 100,000 m'/d
under dry-year conditions from the Luduan area of the aquifer, which is located along the
Daling River some 20 kan to the east of Jinzhou. The aquifer is recharged over part of its
length through connections with surface water flows in Daling River.
39.         The component would provide an additional 100,000 m3/d of water to
ruizhou, tlus reducing the anticipated shortfall in year 2000. In addition, there would be
enhancements to the distribution system, water treatment plant and related facilities and a
new tansmission main to provide additional water to the Jinmi Port City.
40.         Proposed Component ($22.2 milllon). The works to be implemented under

(b) Baduan Booster Pump Station comprising reservoirs pumping plant,

100,000 m3/d;

about 100,000 m3/d;

Jincheng Paper Mill Pollution Management
41.         The Jincheng paper mill produces 100,000 tons per year of paper and board
using reed as the raw material. The production process is inefficient and highly polluting
and the pollution load of the 65,000 m3/d wastewater discharge from the mill to the Daling
River is equivalent to that of the wastewater from a population of 3 million. The discharge
from the mill is tie largest single discharge to the Daling, and there is concern in terms
of the potential effect of this pollution on the quality of groundwater recharged by the
river.
42.         The objective of the component is to improve the efficiency of water use in
the mill, by means of wastewater treatment, recycling and process modifications, and to
recover both process raw materials and concentrated process liquor from the pulping
operations (the so-called red liquor) for sale as a lignosulfonate binder material. White
water from the paper-malkng plant would be treated by coagulation/filtration for recovery
of fiber and talc and the treated wastewater reused both in the paper-making section and
the pulp mill. Water consumption in the pulp mill would also be reduced by more efficient
use of water in the pulping process, which would have the further benefit of producing a
more concentrated red liquor. This would be further concentrated to a level of 50 percent
dissolved solids by means of multiple-effect evaporation.
43.         The component would reduce water consumption by about 40,000 m3/d, of
which 22,000 mrr3/d is in paper-maldng and 18,000 m3/d is in the pulp mill. In addition,
there would be recovery of 6,000 tons per year of paper fiber and 8,000 tons per year of
talc and produce a total of 150,000 tons per year of binder.
44.         Proposed Component ($16.5 million). The works to be implemented under
this component are:
(a)   Red Uquor Extraction comprising double-roll press equipment and
associated facilities;
(b)   Red Liquor Evaporation comprsing evaporators and associated equipment
for producing 150,000 tons per year of lignosulfonate binder product;



- 78 -                         ANNEX 3
(c)   White Water Recovery comprising equipment and facilities for recovery
of about 6,000 tons per year of fiber and 8,000 tons per year of talc for
reuse. About 40,000 m3/d of water would be recovered for reuse; and
(d)   Fuelwood Production comprising press equipment for salvage of waste
fiber for reuse as boiler fuel.

benefit analysis; economic instruments; effects of market economics on
environmental management;
(c)   pollution control-waste minimization in industry; industrial wast
recycling; reuse and recovery; water conservation; waste and wastewater
treatment technology; and
(d) environmental monitoring-objectives and designs of monitoring programs;
quality control of sampling and analysis; computerized data management.
54.        The program is expected to include: lecture courses, hands-on tWaining,
workshops in key environmental areas, and overseas training. The training needs
asessment would be undertaken in collaboration with the Liaoning EPB and would identify
equipment to be provided for the environmental training center in Shenyang. The program
would be implemented in Phase II, which it is expected would be undertaken over a period
of 18 months.
On=  FUIn   PROJECr PREPARATON
55.        This would provide for the formulation and preparation of future investment
prects yet unidentified.

- 106 -                        ANNEX 7
LAD ACQUISMON AND RESE1VHEMENT PLAN
Overall Preparation of Resettlement Action Plans
1.          Prior to appraisal, all project cities presented the Bank with resettlement
plans for those project components requiring land acquisition. Prior to negotiations, the
Liaoning Provincial Govemment (LPG) forwarded to the Bank an updated and acceptable
land acquisition and resettlement plan. All project cities-Anshan, Benxi, Dalian, Fushun,
and Jinzhou-have such components.
2.          The resettlement plans for individual cities share many features, due to the
fact that all were developed within the same regulatory framework (described in Chapter 2
of China: Involuntary Resettlement, Report No. 11641-CHA). The Bank review of
Chinese resettlement policy showed that basing compensation on collective land ownership
(for rural communities) or enterprises (in urban areas) effectively protected the interests
of all groups but the unregistered population (migrants who have not been given the right
of permanent abode). Project cities contend, and site visits by Bank staff yielded no
evidence, that no members of the unregistered population depend on the land acquired for
this project.
3.          In each city, the resettlement efforts would be executed by the city land
administration bureau, or another government agency with special responsibility for
resettlement. All project cities have massive investment programs that involve substantial
rsettlement and the assigned agencies are therefore experienced in this work. The
executing agencies are those typically used in resettlement work and acknowledged in the
Bank's resettlement review to be well placed to execute the work. Each would be required
to submit annual reports on their efforts under the Bank project. Supervision would be
provided by Bank staff.
4.          In addition to the discussions with the provincial project office, preappraisal
and appraisal missions conducted separate discussions and field trips among all
subcomponents in order to understand the basic scope and preparation status of land
requisition and resettlement. A brief summary follows of the major mission findings. The
table at the end summarizes the land and other assets to be acquired and compensation
paid. The resettlement plans themselves can be found in the Project File.
Anshan Wastewater Treatment Plant
5.          The proposed wastewater treatment plant site adjoins an Anshan Iron and
Steel Company industrial solid waste dump. The 18-ha site currently supports irrigated
agriculture, producing one crop of rice annually. The intercepter would be built in the



- 107 -                        ANNEX 7
existing drainage canal and therefore requires no additional land acquisition. Consistent
with the resettlement plan, no structures were found in the area. The area to be acquired
falls within the boundaries of a single village and takes approximately one fourth of the
cultivated land in that village.
6.          Because land acquisition would not require any housing removal, nor affect
any productive enterprise or employment off the land, the social and economic impact of
resettlement would be limited to the losses inherent in the land. Communal ownership
assures that the land acquisition would not result in any family losing its land base.
Rather, all families would suffer a 25 percent reduction in cultivated land. Anshan
municipality estimated the gross output value of the rice at Y 9,000 per ha. This figure
stands well above the provincial average of Y 7,500 for rice, presumably due to relatively
high input use. Farmers 1ose net, not gross, income when they lose the land. Using the
provincial average ratio of net to gross (based on purchased inputs, not including own
labor), the Anshan farm families forgo approximately Y 5,135 per ha in income. The
compensation proposed by the project includes Y 300,000 per ha paid to the village, or
nearly 60 times the annual net income from the land. Currently, bank term-savings
deposits yield slightly over 10 percent, or over Y 30,000 per ha, so such risk-free use of
the funds would result in a substantial increase in real income to affected families. In
addition, the labor previously used on the land would be freed for other productive
purposes. The mission judges that this compensation level fully meets the requirement of
maintaining income at before-resettlement levels.
Benid Wastewater Treatment Plant
7.          The collectors and interceptor would be laid in the watercourses currently
serving as open sewers and drains. No land need be acquired for that purpose and
watercourses would remain as drains for storm water. The treatment plant itself would be
located on land acquired a decade ago for a nursery. Some 15 ha are on a river floodplain
that became usable due to the recent completion of an upstream reservoir that prevents
flooding. Before reservoir completion, seasonal flooding prevented use of the land for
cultivation and it is currently covered with brush. A further 10 ha would require
destruction of orchards. In addition to the land acquired, three families would lose their
houses to the project.
8.         The ftree families have been offered, and accepted, new housing sites some
500 m from their current location. The sites adjoin one another, as did the original sites,
and equal the original sites in size. The owners would be expected to demolish their own
houses, with full salvage rights, and manage construction of their new housing. In addition
to compensation adequate to rebuild housing to the original standard, each family would
be granted Y 1,000 for removal costs and Y 1,200 as a transition period living subsidy.
The latter sum equals 14 months' per capita income for the families.
9.          The nursery is a state, as opposed to collective, enterprise. The land
acquisition would not, therefore, result in the loss of cultivated land to any particular
family. The nursery has uncultivated land suitable for the reestablishment of the 6 ha of



- 108 -                        ANNEX 7
orchard to be lost. The compensation negotiated by the enterprise to protect itself (and
hence all workers) from economic loss totals Y 523,500 per ha. Current income per ha
from the orchards totals Y 17,255. The available funds would allow full reestablishment
of 6 ha of orchard, compensate for all income loss during the five-year period needed to
regain full production, provide an additional margin for risk, and leave the nursery with
a younger orchard. The compensation package is judged to fully meet the shared Bank and
Chinese goals of protecting project-affected people from adverse effects.
Dalian Malan River Wastewater Treatment Plant
10.        The proposed Malan River Wastewater Treatment Plant is located along the
Malan River in the southern coastal area of Dalian. It would require 13 ha of land in an
urban area. No farmland would be affected and the land in question is government owned,
but eight factories and commercial enterprises would be displaced. Not atypically for
Chinese industry, employee housing is provided on factory grounds and factory relocation
would nev..ssitate the relocation of 85 families. The largest affected enterprise is the
Dalian Chemical Plant with over 300 employees.
11.        Dalian has developed a resettlement plan for the industrial enterprises that
relocates the three chemical plants to the new Nanguanling chemical industries district,
19 kn from their present site; the two construction materials sales companies would go to
the Sandaogou zone, 14 km from the current site; a specialty oil supply firmn would
relocate 6 km to the Xishancun oil depot; an aquaculture company warehouse would move
11 km to the mouth of the Lingshui river; and the labor bureau of a shipbuilding firm
would move 9.6 km to a space off Yanhai Road. All would have their new facilities
constructed before the move so as to minimize disruption to their operations and aU
employees would continue to receive full pay over the move period.
12.        The 85 families needing to be rehoused would be given apartments in a new
housing development in the current neighborhood, with no temporary housing needed.
This move would ensure that they can continue to use the same schools and other public
facilities to which they are accustomed. It would, however, substantialy increase the
commuting distance for family members employed in the factory, for they would now need
to travel 19 km to work. The factory is planning to provide a home-to-work bus for these
people, which would help ease the burden. Other family members, of course, would have
unchanged commutes.
Fushun Wastewater Treatment Plant
13.        The proposed wastewater treatment plant would occupy 11 ha of irrigated
farmland currently under a coir-ination of paddy and maize and the village that adjoins
that land. A total of 70 village   ;ies would need relocation. Another 2.4 ha would be
acquired along a 3.4-km-long sec .n of the interceptor. The latter area would consist of
a strip of land paralleling the current drainage canal and is a mixture of cultivated land and
farm housing. Use of this land would displace 79 families. The remaining section of the
intercepter would be in a trench along the riverbed and would not affect productive land.



-109 -                         ANNEX 7
Construction of branch sewers would require the relocation of an additional 39 families,
for a total of 188 families needing relocation. In addition to the permanent land taken, an
additional 16 ha of cultivated land would be temporarily used dtiring construction, then
returned to the cultivators.
14.        The project office would provide new housing or housing sites for all
families needing relocation. Following the pattern in urban resettlement, for those
currently in government housing, the new housing would provide substantially more floor
space and improved amenities. The project office estimates an average 27 percent increase
in floor space for each family as well as amenities such as private flush toilets, now
available in few of the affected households. These improvements come at the price of
physical uislocation, with the new housing located 2 to 4 km from the original housing
site. For the 80 percent of the affected families, all from farm villages who own their own
housing, the city would provide new housing plots on which the farmers can rebuild. The
land would require a nominal Y 10 per year (less than $2) use right payment. Housing
would be compensated at a level permitting the construction of new housing of area equal
to the original.
15.        The acquisition of cultivated land would displace 226 farmers. Because of
the amnount of land lost and the physical displacement of villagers from the remaining land,
all farmers would shift to nonagricultural status. With this status comes access to the
urban public welfare system and, for resettling people, state responsibility for providing
employment. Of the 226, 36 would be employed by the wastewater treatment plant. The
remaining 190 would have their employment arranged by the Fushun labor bureau. For
the period until such employment, which may take up to 30 months, the farmers would be
employed by the labor bureau and assigned to temporary labor jobs or, once the permanent
position has been identified, taining courses for their new jobs.
16.        Employment would be funded through compensation for lost land.
Compensation levels vary by land use, hence income. Payment from the project to the
municipality for vegetable land would be Y 1.6 million per ha, irrigated land at Y 380,000
per ha, and rainfed land at Y 298,000 per ha. Those figures include both compensation
for lost production and special taxes designed to discourage land acquisition. Because the
communities themselves would not arrange alternative employment, they would receive no
more than Y 54,000 per ha for irrigated land and Y 45,000 per ha for rainfed land. The
remaining funds would be used by the labor bureau for investment in enterprises providing
jobs for the displaced labor. In Fushun, such provide an average income of no less than
Y 4,800 per year in direct salary and subsidies, well above the average net annual crop
income per farmer of Y 800.
17.        Despite the increases in housing space or quality and the higher incomes
enjoyed by resettled farmers, the welfare gain necessarily remains ambiguous. The
substantial shift in lifestyle, in moving from independent farming to more regimented
industrial manual labor, would not necessarily be welcomed by every affected family.
Some opportunity remains for distributing these opportunities among collective members
by preference, as some land remainis in each affected village, but the assumption is that



-110 -                         AN X
those losing housing would move. They would be able to remain only if families not
losing housing wouldingly trade their housing for a city apartment and the new job
opportunity. Those decisions are made by the community, not by the resettlement office
and no guarantee can be given that a family preferring to remain in farming would be
allowed to do so.
18.        Farmers having land taken for temporary project use would be compensated
for the full gross output value of their land during the entire use period. Ihis more than
compensates for forgone income, because they need not purchase inputs for that land nor
apply their labor to it. If the temporary use involves disturbing soil structure (digging, as
opposed to spoil placement), then additional compensation is paid for the period needed
to return the land to its original productivity. Compensation levels are Y 13,000/year for
vegetable land, Y 8,800/year for irrigated land, and Y 3,900/year for rainfed land.
Jinzhou Water Supply Project
19.        The Jinzhou Water Supply Project consists of a wellfield, pump station,
water distribution plant, a 25-kn-long water pipeline and access roads. The total project
would acquire nearly 17 ha of farmland and temporarily use a further 99 ha. The bulk of
this land is rainfed grain land in Songshan and Xingzhuang townships. A small proportion
is used for vegetable cultivation or afforested.
20.         The Jinzhou situation resembles that of Anshan in that land acquisition would
not require any housing removal, nor affect any productive enterprise or employment off
the land, therefore limiting the social and economic impact of resettlement to the losses
inherent in the land. Again, communal ownership assures that the land acquisition would
not result in any family losing its land base. Indeed, the community itself would lose a
much lower percentage of its land than in Anshan, with the most affected community
losing less hn 10 percent of its cultivated land. The project is basing compensation on
gross income from cultivated land totaling Y 9,000 per ha for irrigated land and Y 7,500
per ha for rainfed land. These nominal figures are above actual returns as reported by the
villages. The Anshan calculation for net income holds here as well, suggesting a net of
approximately Y 5,135 per ha for irrigated land and Y 4,300 per ha for rainfed. Direct
compensation to the villages would total Y 81,000 per ha for irrigated land and Y 67,500
per ha for rainfed, in each case over 15 times the net income from the land. Again, with
risk-free bank term-savings deposits yielding slightly over 10 percent, the equivalent
income would total Y 8,400 per year for irrigated land and Y 7,000 for rainfed. In
addition, the labor previously used on the land would be freed for other productive
purposes. This compensation level is judged to fully meet the requirement of maintaining
income at before-resettlement levels.
21.         Temporarily acquired land would be compensated for its gross output value
during the period of use, again with a premium paid if the structure of the land is
disturbed. Specifically, land compacted by vehicle traffic would be paid an extra year's
full income as additional compensation and land excavated would be paid an additional



-111-                                    ANNEX 7
eight years' full income. This compensation level is judged to fully meet the requirement
of protecting income of the temporarily affected people.
22.            Trees on land taken for either permanent or temporary use would be
compensated additionally to the normal land compensation, based on their full value.
Moreover, farmers would be permitted to salvage the trees.

E ONMENTAL ASSESSMENT SM
hItroduction
1.          Liaoning Province is located in the northeast of China and is bordered to the
north by Jilin Province, to the east by the Democratic Republic of Korea, to the south by
the Bohai Sea and to the west by Hebei Province and the Inner Mongolia Autonomous
Region. The province has a total land area of 145,700 km2 and a population of 36 million,
of which 25 million are urban, and has developed a strong industrial base, many of the
cities being major centers of heavy industry. Basic food supplies are derived from
agriculture carried out in several large river basins, principally the twin basins of the Hun
and Taizi Rivers in the heardand of the province and occupying some 20 percent of its land
but producing about 40 percent of its gross agricultural output. These same basins contain
more than one third of the population of Liaoning and produce about 60 percent of its
gross induswtrial output.
2.          Historic rapid industrial development, coupled with inadequate wastewater
mnanagement, has seriously threatened the existing limited water resources, and substantial
inmreases in industrial production are planned. The total quantity of wastewater discharged
from the six major cities in the Hun-Taizi Basin have been estimated at 2.4 million m3/d
in 1987 and are projected to increase to 4.4 million m3/d in 2000. In addition, independent
discharges from major industries are estimated to rise from 2.5 million m3/d in 1987 to
3.8 million m3/d in 2000. Such increases would further degrade the limited water
resources of the province.
3.          Water consumption in all cities is dominated by industrial use, which
typically accounts for about 70 percent of consumption. Discharges of pollution from
industry are frequently associated with inadequately controlled and therefore inefficient and
wasteful use of both water and materials. Water consumption per unit of industrial output
is frequently very high by intemational standards. Studies of diversion of water from
catchments where there are, albeit modest, surpluses to augment or substitute existing
polluted resources have indicated that unit costs are very substantial and in some cases
exorbitant. Thus, there is a clear need, in addition to more effective wastewater
management, for industry to improve the efficiency of water use if industrial growth is to
be sustained. Indeed, there is evidence that industrial output in some cities is already
constained by water resource restrictions.
4.          Similar lack of controls on polluting discharges and the inefficient use of
resources are also causing severe problems of air pollution in many of the major cities in
the province, notably in the city of Benxi. The problems are derived principally from the
combustion of poor-quality coal for heating, power generation and industrial use and result



- 113 -                        A
in extremely poor urban air quality, with substantial exceedance of even the least-stringent
air quality criteria. The nature and extent of the problems are such that they cannot be
solved at a reasonable cost and wifhin a realistic timeframe solely by the provision of
emission controls. There would need to be a "cradle to grave' approach to achieve
pollution reduc,ins at all stages ranging from fuel sourcing to controls on combustion.
S.          The effective utilization of water resources in the Hun-Taizi Basin was the
sul,;ect of a previous study, the Hun-Taizi River Basin Management Study (HTRBMS),
managed by the Bank and funded by the Australian International Development Assistance
Bureau (AIDAB). The study was completed in 1988 and produced a ranked set of
investments for water resource development and water pollution control measures designed
to improve water resource utilization in the Basin. A number of water resource
developments were included in the Bank-financed Liaoning Urban Infrastructure Project
and the proposed project would finance, inter alia, the second set of priority investments
identified by HTRBMS focused on water pollution abatement.
6.         In order to address the concerns described above, the proposed project would
fscus on improving the state of the environment in Liaoning via a range of investments
with the objectives of:
(a)  improving water quality, principally in the Hun-Taizi Basin, to allow safe
beneficial use;
0b)  improving urban air quality;
(c)  improving standards of municipal wastes management;
(d)  institution of measures to alleviate industrial pollution and to improve water
and materials udlization; and
(e)   strengthening of policies and institutional arrangements for water and air
quality management, wastewater facilities operations, environmental
regulation and management training.
7.          Technical support and training would be provided to various environment
sector agencies in Liaoning and both provincial and municipal level including environment
protection bureaus (EPBs) and municipal utility operations and finance departments.
Administrtive and Institutional Framework
8.          The State Environmental Protection Comminttee (SEPC) is the highest level
of authority on environmental policy and includes the State Council and heads of all
relevant ministries and agencies. The National Environmental Protection Agency (NEPA)
functions as the secretriat of SEPC and is responsible for all aspects of environmental
policy although it shares authority with other agencies for certain natual resources. NEPA
sets overall policies and regulations governing the provincial and municipal environmental



-114 -                          ANNEX 8
protection bureaus (EPBs) and implementation of environmental policy is through the
municipal and provincial EPBs, who are responsible for the maintenance of environmental
quality.
9.          Specific responsibility for water resources in Liaoning is shared between five
agencies, coordinated by the Liaoning Water Resource Management Committee headed by
a Vice Governor of the province. Maintenance of water quality is the responsibility of the
Liaoning EPB and its subordinate municipal EPBs. Trose bureaus monitor environmental
quality, set environmental and discharge standards, assess and levy pollution charges and
prosecute serious polluters. All discharges to watercourses in Liaoning, whether from the
cities or from industry, come under the control of the EPBs.
Project Description
10.         The proposed project comprises a total of 12 components as follows:
(a)   Anshan Wastewater Treatment and Recovery-physicochemical treatment of
220,000 m3/d of wastewater largely from the ANGANG steel complex and
recovery of the treated wastewater for process use in the complex;
(b)   Benxi Wastewater Treatment-provision of trunk sewers and chemically
assisted primary treatment plant for 300,000 m3/d of mixed municipal and
industrial wastewater;
(c)   Fushun Wastewater Treatment-provision of trunk sewer system  and
chemically assisted primary treatment plant for 250,000 m3/d of mixed
municipal and industrial wastewater;
(d)   Benxi Air Quality Management-retrofitting of emission controls in the form
of dry electrostatic precipitators at two blast furnaces (replacing existing wet
scrubber systems) and controls on coal loading and unloading at three coke
ovens in the Benxi Iron and Steel complex to reduce emissions, and in the
former case, permit heat recovery from waste gases; provision of coal-fired
boilers and distribution pipework for a new district heating system;
(e)   Dalian Wastewater Treatment and Recovery-provision of Malan River
trunk sewer system and secondary treatment plant for 120,000 m3/d of
mixed municipal and industrial wastewater; distribution system for recovery
of treated wastewater for use by lo.al industry; sewerage system
improvements and upgrading of Chunliu wastewater treatment plant to
increase treatment capacity to 60,000 m3/d to enhance industrial reuse of
treated wastewater;
(f)   Dalian Solid Wastes Management-improvements to solid waste collection
facilities; construction of new waste transfer station and provision of bulk



- 115 -                        ANNEX 8
waste transport vehicles; development of landfill site with leachate control
and landfill gas collection facilities;
(g)   Jinzhou Water Supply-development of new groundwater resources to
substitute existing boreholes close to the city that have become polluted;
(h)   Jincheng Paper Mill Process Improvements-reduction in pollution load
(currently 3 million population equivalent) from paper mill by process
improvements comprising: water recycling; improvements in process
chemical utilization; and recovery of a lignosulfonate binder product for
various industrial applications;
(i)   Industrial Water Conservation-various projects in Dalian to reduce water
consumption in industry, institutional use, and water utility (improved leak
detection);
.j)   Environmental Rehabilitation and Construction-improved conservation and
presentation of Liaoning Provincial Museum, Niuheliang, Jiumenkou Great
Wall and Jieshi Gong.
(k)   Environmental Protection Fund-a fund similar to those included in other
Bank-financed environment and infrastructure projects in China focused on
industrial pollution control and process improvement projects; and
({)   Technical Assistance and Training Components-including institutional
strengthening; project management; financial management and economic
analysis; training for wastewater treatment and wastes management
operations; pilot wastewater treatment plant; and energy policy study for
Benxi.
11.        Of the above components, (a)-(h) involve physical works in the immediate
term and are therefore covered by the EA studies. The components are divided within
three distnct geographic areas within Liaoning as follows:
Hun-Taiz; River Basin/Central Liaoning                         a-d
Xiaoling-Daling River Basin/SE Liaoning                      e & f
DaLian area (Liaodong peninsula)/S Liaoning                  g & h
The EA for the project as a whole is subdivided to reflect these three geographic areas.



- 116 -                        ANNE  8
Baseline Data
12.         General. Liaoning Province has important coal, oil, and iron ore reserves
that have enabled it to become a major industrial center of China, generating about
7 percent of national industrial output. A number of cities in Liaoning are centers of
heavy industry of national importance. The importance of industry is reflected in the fact
that, although Liaoning has also a significant agricultural output, there has been high
population growth in the cities as a result of migration from rural areas. Some cities such
as Dalian are establishing special economic development zones, which are increasing the
rate of industrial development.
13.         Principal economic activities in the project area include: coal mining; oil
and gas production; petroleum refining; chemicals manufacture; steel and coke production;
nachinery manufacture; metallurgy; pulp and paper production; textiles and light industry.
14.         Climate. The climate in the project area of Liaoning is subhumid, with
maritime influences resulting in a moderation of temperatures, more so in Dalian than in
other project cities. Annual average daily temperatures range from 60C to 90C. The
coldest month is January, with daily average temperatures ranging between -5C and
-17C, and July, the hottest month, has daily average temperatures between 230C and
240C.
15.         Average annual precipitawion ranges between 500 mm and 1,000 mm,
increasing from southeast to northwest. Between 63 and 70 percent of precipitation occurs
as rain during the summer mcvths of June to September, with approximately 9 to
10 percent falling in the winter months of December to February.
16.         Ecology. Upland forested areas of Liaoning contain poplar, larch, willow,
oak, dragon spruce, fir and northeast China ash; fauna include badger, roe deer, pheasant,
and egret. The project components are, however, located in urban or agricultural areas
where the majority of the native flora and fauna have been replaced by species adaptable
to such environments.
17.         Wastewater discharges have impaired riverine aquatic environments in the
Hun-Taizi Basin (Anshan, Benxi, Fushun discharges) and the Daling Basin (Jinzhou and
Jincheng discharges). In areas of acute pollution, there are reportedly no fish species
present, although in less polluted areas carp, catfish and wild gill eel are found. Offshore
areas around Dalian are diverse, the Heishijiao Bight and Dalian Bay being rich marine
environments supporting numerous native species and highly productive aquaculture
systems. Major cultivated species include kelp, abalone, scallops and mussels. However,
in the Heishijiao Bight close to the mouth of the Malan River, the environment has been
impaired by wastewater discharges. Areas of Jinzhou Bay originally contained mud flats
with native populations of alkaline rush and reeds, but many of these mud flats have been
converted for prawn farming.



- 117 -                          ANNEX 8
18.         Water Quality. Water quality standards for China have been developed by
NEPA and are known as the Environmental Quality Standards for Surface Waters
(EQSSW). For rivers, the EQSSW are applicable for water quality in the river
downstream of any mixing zones with polluting discharges. EQSSW are defined for five
water use classifications, for each of which a set of maximum permissible concentrations
of various pollutants. The water use classifications are listed below, and the applicable
EQSSW in Annex 2.
a     Class I-very clean waters, for natural protection.
*     Class 11-water used for drinking water source.
*     Class m-water used for drinking water after some treatment.
*     Class IV-water used for recreational use, boating, fishing and for industrial
water supply.
a     Class V-water suitable for industrial cooling water or for irrigation.
The water quality targets for the Hun-Taizi and Daling Rivers that are affected by the
various project components are shown in Table 1.
19.         Wastewater discharges, both municipal and industrial, must comply with the
requirements of the national Integrated Wastewater Discharge Standards (IWDS), which
have been modified to take account of the specific environmental requirements of Liaoning.
The Liaoning standards are listed in Annex 2 and are generally more stringent than IWDS
and were implemented in 1990. Wastewater must be treated to maintain one of two
standards based on the beneficial uses of the receiving water:
*     Standard I-for discharge to Class III surface water.
o     Standard 11-for discharge to Class IV or Class V surface water.
20.         In no instance may discharges be made to Class I or Class II surface water
bodies. The Liaoning standards also include conditions on flow, water reuse rate and
maximum concentrations of a number of pollutants specifically for wastewaters from
24 categories of industry, principally heavy industry.
21.         The National Marine Water Classification system classifies manne waters
are classified into three categories as a function of water use as follows:
a     Class I-natural protection, salt harvesting, fisheries
o     Class 11-recreation
     Class m-industrial uses, harbots

22.             As for discharges to freshwater, there are two standards in Liaoning for
wastewater discharges to marine waters depending upon the beneficial uses of the receiving
water:
e       Standard I-for discharge to Class II waters
e       Standard 11-for discharge to Class m  waters
In no case is a wastewater discharge to Class I waters permitted. Details of the Liaoning
standards for discharge to marine waters are given in the Project File.
23.             The Hun-Taizi Rivers generally flow in a northeast to southwest direction
through the province and discharge some 98 kn downstream of their confluence into the
Bohai Sea via the Gulf of Liaodong. The rivers are heavily exploited for a number of
uses, including agiculture, and the flow regime highly influenced by the operation of large
multipurpose impounding reservoirs. The Liaoning EPB monitors water quality in the
basin at 23 locations at frequencies that are seasonal and based on nver flow conditions.



- 119 -                        ANNEX 8
The upper reaches of the rivers are generally of high quality, but water quality deteriorates
as the rivers flow through th_ more developed regions of the province. Most of the
surface waters in the basin within the developed areas are of very poor quality, failing to
comply even with the Class V standards. The problem is compounded during the dry
season when virtually the entire river flows consist of raw wastewater, and groundwater
has become contaminated via surface water recharge.
24.         The use of these polluted water sources for potable supply poses potential
problems in terms of threats to human health. The poor quality of surface water
downstream of Fushun and Benxi also adversely affects agricultural irrigation, and
irrigation standards are exceeded in terms of concentrations of COD, oil and ammonia.
25.         The Daling-Xiaoling basin is the largest catchment of the rivers in the
Jinzhou administrative area. Flows in the rivers and tributaries are dominated by runoff
resulting from precipitation and flows are therefore highly variable. In the case of the
Daling, the monthly average flows range from about 9 m3/s in January to more than
150 m3/s in July and August. Most rivers in the basin flow through areas of hilly
topography with steep slopes and limited vegetative cover, and as a result there is severe
erosion with subsequent sedimentation and siltation in the downstream rivers.
26.         The Daling rises in Jianchang, a hilly area in the southwest of Jinzhou and
discharges to the Gulf of Liaodong some 400 river km downstream. As a result of
erosion, water quality in the upper reaches of the river is poor in terms of suspended
solids. In addition, there are also discharges of pollution to the river, in particular that
from the Jincheng Paper Mill, which has a pollution load of some 3 million population
equivalent. The dilution of this discharge ranges from about 200 in July/August to as little
as 12 in January. As a result, COD concentrations in the Daling are in the order of
hundreds of mg/l. The effect of the discharge from the Jincheng Paper Mill alone is to
increase the COD concentration in the Daling by up to about 200 mg/l depending upon the
river flow.
27.         Groundwater in the urban area of Jinzhou City is mainly derived from water-
bearing strata alkng the banks of the Xiaoling and Nuer rivers. Yields are limited and
there is evidence of contamination of some wells as a result of polluting discharges by
industry. The remaining groundwater resources in the region of Jinzhou are in the Daling
and Xiaoling alluvial fans with water-bearing strata consisting of gritstones with thickness
between 20 and 60 m.
28.         The Malan River in Dalian is 14 km in length with adrainage area of
95 km2 and discharges to the Yellow Sea via the Heishijiao Bight. It constitutes the major
outlet for wastewater in the southwest of Dalian and receives discharges totaling up to
50,000 m3/d from more than 100 industrial plants. The discharge from the Malan River
is causing pollution problems along the adjacent shoreline of the Heishijiao Bight, which
is a popular area for tourism. Elsewhere in Heishijiao Bight, seawater quality is generally
good.



- 120 -                        ANNEX
29.         Shouyu Bay, part of Daman Bay, to the northeast of Dalian also receives
untreated municipal and industrial wastewater discharges. These discharges, together with
the restricted water movement in the bay, are reported to be causing eutrophication
problems, and Shouyu Bay is considered to be the most polluted area of Dalian Bay.
30.         Mr Quality. Ambient air quality standards in China are based on three
clssifications for air quality as follows:
o     Class I-protection of human health and ecological resources based on long-
term exposure to contaminants.
e     Class 11-protection of human health and ecological resources based on
long- and short-term exposure to contaminants.
0    Class m-minimum standard for protection of human health and ecological
resources based on acute and chronic exposure to contaminants.
The standards include concentrations of particulates (TSP), sulfur dioxiJe (SO,), nitrogen
oxides (NO), carbon dioxide and photochemical products and are given in Annex 2.
31.         The City of Benxi has the poorest air quality of any city in Liaoning and
probably in China. Air quality is monitored at six locations in Benxi considered to
reresent the most likely arithmetic average air quality to which inhabitants of Benxi are
exposed and at a seventh location considered to represent background conditions. The air
quality data for SO% and TSP for 1990 are given in Tables 2 and 3. Measured air quality
varies as a function of sampling location and seasonally, and is particularly poor in winter,
when SO concentrations rise by up to an order of magnitude. Concentrations of SO2 and
TSP substantially exceed even the Class m air quality standards.
32.         The poor air quality in Benxi is largely as a result of the combustion of coal
of poor quality (m terms of high sulfur and ash contents) by industry, for power generation
and heating and of the widespread absence of emission controls on discharges to
atmosphere. Total consumption of coal in Benxi is of the order of 7.5 million tons/year
and the major emissions of SO2 and TSP are from power generation, iron and steel
production (blast furnaces and coke ovens) and cement manufacture. Total emissions of
SO2 and TSP have been estimated for 1991 at more than 140,000 and 220,000 tons/year
(a major proportion of which is accounted for by fugitive emissions), respectively. Benxi
has a Master Plan for Air Pollution Abatement with the objective of achieving Class m air
quality for SO2 and Class II for all other pollutants by 2000. To date, this has
concentraed primarily on reducing emissions of TSP. These are expected to reduce by
of the order of 11 percent from the 1991 figure as a result of initiatives already in hand
in terms of emission controls at power plants.
33.         Ihe air quality situation in Benxi is exacerbated by the location of the city
in a river valley surrounded by hills. The formation of stable temperature inversions

34.               Waste Mnagement.  Waste management throughout the Province is
inefficient and has adverse effects upon the environment.  Waste collection and transport
frequently uses small vehicles and involves multiple handling of small quantities of waste,



-122 -                         ANNEX 8
and standards of hygiene are poor. Waste disposal is largely by simple dumping with very
limited control, and there are no sites operated to international standards of sanitary
landfill. As a result, there are problems of pollution of groundwater.
Consideration of Alternatives
35.         In some cases, the options selected represent the only practicable solution
to the specific problem involved. For example, the cost of achieving the very substantial
pollution reductions achieved by process improvements at the Jincheng Paper Mill by
wastewater treatment involving no revenue generation by virtue of product recovery would
have been prohibitively expensive. For cases where there were realistic alternative
options, the rationale for the selection of the proposed selection is described below.
36.         Hun-Talzi Basin Wastewater Treatment. The wastewater treatment plants
proposed for Anshan, Benxi and Fushun are based on primary sedimentation, chemically
assisted to enhance process performance. In the case of Anshan, this was the only process
sequence that could achieve the required treated water quality, given the nature of the raw
wastewater. Although the lack of dilution in the rivers in the basin means that a high
degree of treatment is needed to maintain river water quality, this process sequence was
selected in the immediate term for Benxi and Fushun in preference to biological treatment
systems for the following reasons:
(a)   the mixed wastewater is dilute, reflecting the large contribution by industry
to wastewater flows and probably also inefficient use of water, which would
make biological treatment systems less cost-effective;
(b)  the current lack of rigorous control of industrial wastewaters means that the
mixed wastewater may contain significant concentrations of toxic materials
that could adversely affect biological treatment;
(c)   chemical treatment systems are less temperature sensitive and there are not
currently established design parameters for full-scale biological treatnent
systems under Liaoning winter conditions (a large pilot plant is proposed for
Fushun to undertake the appropriate experimentation); the sustained low
temperatures (as low as -30C) in 1 .iaoning during winter months precludes
the use of waste stabilization ponds in view of the very large areas of land
that would be necessary; and
(d)   the system selected has a lower unit capital cost, which means that a greater
volume of wastewater can be treated for a given level of expenditure and the
cost per unit mass of pollutant removed thus reduced; for the same level of
investment, a much smaller flow could have been treated by biological
treatment and, although this would have been to a higher standard,
substantial volumes of wastewater would have remained untreated and the
overall pollution load removed therefore much smaller.



- 123 -                        ANNEX 8
37.         It is expected that in fuure biological treatmnent would be introduced when
the problems outined in (a) and 0) above have been overcome, and the facilities provided
in LEP would stiU form part of the overall process sequence.
38.         Dalian Wastewater Treatment.  The process proposed for the two
wastewater treatment plants in DaLian is biological treatment using the activated sludge
process. In the case of the existing Chunliu plant, this represents an extension to and
refurbishment of an existing process sequence. Moreover, for both the Chunliu and the
new Malan River plants, biological treatment is the only realistic treatment process
sequence that can achieve a treated wastewater quality suitable for recovery for use by
industry.
39.         An alternative option was investigated for the Malan River in the form of
a pimary treatment plant and discharge to the Heishijiao Bight via a long marine outfafl.
This was rejected because of the cost of the very long outfall (6 km) necessary to provide
adequate dilution and dispersion of the discharge so that water quality in the aquaculture
areas of the Heishijiao Bight were not fthreatned.
40.         Benxi Air Quality  nagement. Only in the case of the emissions control
for coke oven loading and unloading was there an alternative process option. The option
proposed is not the least-cost option and was selected because the alternative, based on less
complicated process technology, was not approved by Benxi EPB because it could only
achieve 94 percent solids removal compared with the 98 percent removed by the more
complex system and required by Benxi EPB.
41.         Dal'an Solid Waste Management. Incineration and composting were
investgated as alteratives to landfill, and were rejected, respectively, on grounds of cost
and lack of demand for the product. In either case, there would still be a need for landfill
of incinerator ash or compost plant reject streams.
Enviromnental Benefts
42.         Hun-Taizi River Basin. The wastewater treatment projects for cities in the
Hun-Taizi basin would provide substantial environmental benefits in terms of reduced
pollution loads discharges to the rivers and in the case of Anshan complete removal of
wastewater from the receiving watercourse. The benefits associated with the individual
project components in the Hun-Taizi Basin are discussed below.
43.         Anshan. The treatment plant at Anshan would treat 220,000 me/d from the
Xi Da Gou channel, one of four channels that discharge to the Yunliang River, a tributary
of the Taizi. The flow in the Xi Da Gou consists almost entirely of industrial wastewater
and typically has high concentrations of suspended solids (in excess of 1,000 mg/l) and oil
(in excess of 20 mg/l). This would be treated by a combination of coagulation,
sedimentation and filtration to produce treated effluent complying with the ANGANG steel
plant standards for water for process reuse in the steel plant. This would involve removal
of about 95 percent of suspended solids and oil and would therefore remove more than



- 124- A-NE a
200 tons of suspended solids of industral origin and about 4 tons of oil per day from the
river system. Thus, even on the occasions when the treated wastewater is discharged to
the Xi Da Gou, at times of lack of demand in the steel plant, there would still be a major
improvement in the quality of water downstream that is used in agriculture.
44.         lewd. The city of Benxi is situated on the Taizi direcdy upstream of the
Shenwo reservoir and about 40 km downstream of the Guanyenge reservoir. Wastewater
from the city, both municipal and industrial, is discharged almost entirely without
treatment to the Taizi via a number of tributaries and open channels. The proposed
wastewater interceptor would collect flows in these tributaries and channels over a distance
of some 12 river kn for treatment at a plant downstream of the city. There would be a
substantal improvement in water quality in the Taizi as it traverses the city as a result of
the complete removal of these discharges. Downstream of the city, there would b,' an
improvement by virtue of the pollution load reduction achieved in treatment.
45.         The estimated reduction in COD concentration in the Taizi as it traverses
the city is about 40 percent. The proposed interceptor sewer would not collect wastewater
from a major industrial area including the Benxi Iron and Steel complex, the wastewaters
from which would be collected and treated separately. Such treatment would be necessary
if the proposed water quality standards for the Taizi are to be achieved. A very significant
reduction in pollution from the Benxi Iron and Steel complex would result from the
replacement of the wet scrubbers for blast furnace off-gas by a dry electrostatic precipitator
fcility as described in detail below.
46.         Fushiun. The city of Fushun is located on the Hun River immediately
downsteam of the multipurpose Dahuofang Reservoir and 50 km upstream of Shenyang,
the provincial capital. Fushun is heavily industrialized and some 84 percent of the total
wastewater flow (745,000 m3/d) is derived from industrial sources. Of the total wastewater
flow, about 55 percent is discharged direct to the Hun River and 38 percent to the Shenfu
Irrigation Canal, which runs from west to east and conveys the untreated wastewater to
irrigate some 10,000 ha of farmland.
47.         The project allows for the collection and treatment of mixed municipal and
industial wastewater stream, which excludes wastewater from 20 major industries in
Fushun that produce about 32 percent of the total wastewater flow and would be treated
separtely at source. This was decided from considerations of treatability effects on the
mixed wastewater, treatment economics and the financial capability of the industries
concerned. The treated industrial wastewater from these 20 industries would be collected
by a separate industrial wastewater interceptor discharging to the Shenfu Canal. The
mixed municipal and industrial wastewater would be collected by a 26-km municipal
waswwater interceptor for chemically assisted pnmary treatment at a plant downstream of
the city.
48.         There would be a substantial improvement in water quality in the Hun River
as it traverses urban Fushun because the discharges of waewater would have been
removed completely. There would be a similar improvement in river quality downstream



- 125 -                        ANNIfi
of Fushun by virtue of the pollution load removed by the treatment plant. The estimated
reduction in COD concentrations in the river water is about 70 percent, with significant
reductions also in terms of specific pollutants of industrial origin such as phenols. Water
quality in the Shenfu Canal would also be improved by virtue of the treatment at the
individual industries.
49.         Beni Air Pollution Control. The environmental benefits of the Benxi air
pollution control component are very significant and take three forms as follows:
(a)   Direct benefits to local air quality as a result of emission controls;
(b)   Indirect benefits as a result of recovery of heat, thereby reducing the co*l
consumption necessary for the same heat demand;
(c)   Indirect benefits by virtue of fuel substitution and/or improved combustion
efficiency; the district heating component would replace small inefficient
coal-fired boilers, which are particularly polluting because they burn poor-
quality coal and have no emission controls; moreover, discharge stacks are
short and therefore pollutants are discharged close to ground level with very
limited scope for dispersion.
50.        The replacement of the existing wet scrubbers at the blast furnaces by dry
electrostatic precipitators would result in a small increase in solids removal and additionally
would obviate a wastewater discharge of approximately 4.2 million nm/year containing
toxic pollutants such as cyanides (4.7 tons/year) and phenols (2 tons/year) to the Taizi
River. The principal benefit, however, would be that the blast furnace gas can be used in
coke ovens, thereby displacing coke oven gas for use to supplement the city gas supply.
This would amount to approximately a doubling of the availability of gas for residental
use, with a substantial saving in residential coal consumption. This substitution would
reduce SO% emissions in Benxi by about 1,800 tons/year.
51.         The emission controls at the coke ovens give a relatively small reduction in
emissions of particulates in mass terms, but, since the emissions are fugitive and at ground
level, the improvement in local air quality is substantial. In particular, there is almost
complete elimination of the emissions of highly carcinogenic organic chemicals such as
beazopyrene, which is a significant health hazard to operations personnel at and near the
plant.
52.         The district heating facility gives a very substantial environmental
improvement for two reasons. It would replace a large number of small, inefficient
domestic coal boilers by a large efficient coal-fired combined heat and power plant
equipped with emission controls for removal of both SO and TSP and a number of heat-
only boilers, also coal-fired and equipped with similar emission controls. The expected
reduction in emissions of SO2 is more than 8,000 tons/year for the disrict heating facility
as a whole and about 800 tons/year for the heat-only boilers provided in the component.



- 126 -                        ANNEX 8
53.         The overall total reduction in emissions has been calculated in percentage
terms on adopting the "bubble concept" to Benxi and considering all mass emissions in the
city as equivalent. On this simple and conservative basis, the total reduction in SO2
emissions on an annual basis is approximately 10,000 tons/year (about 7 percent) and that
in TSP emissions is approximately 45,000 tons/year (about 20 percent). In practice, the
effect of the reduction in emissions is likely to be greater, because the reductions are
mainly indirect in respect of reducing the domestic use of coal that is highly seasonal,
mainly for heating in winter. Moreover, the emissions that are being replaced are mainly
from small domestic boilers, where the emissions are probably of the greatest significance
because they are closest to ground level.
54.         Dalian Components. There would be substantial benefits in terms of
receiving water quality as a result of both wastewater treatment components. In the case
of the Malan River plant, all present discharges to the Malan River and thence to the
Heishijiao Bight would be given a high degree of treatment, and there would be a major
improvement in water quality at the mouth of the river and in the adjacent coastal
recreational waters. In addition, any potential threats to water quality in the aquaculture
areas of the Heishijiao Bight would be greatly reduced. In the case of the Chunliu plant
extension, there would be a decrease in the quantities of untreated wastewater discharged
to Dalian Bay in areas where there is limited water movement. In both cases, the recovery
of treated wastewater for industrial use would enhance very limited water resources ir
Dalian.
55.         The development of the Maoyingzi landfill site and the Shouyu Bay refuse
transfer station would improve the aesthetic and environmental standards of wastes
management in Dalian. The transfer station facility is located some 425 km from the
landfill and would substantially improve transport efficiency. The compaction facilities to
be installed and the larger vehicles used for onward transport of wastes to the landfill site
would reduce the number of vehicle movements and therefore the transport-derived
environmental impacts such as traffic, noise and air pollution. Introduction of high
standards of landfill site operation, particularly leachate and landfill gas controls) would
reduce the risk of local groundwater pollution and of gas migration and possible explosion/
fire risks. Moreover, methane is an important greenhouse gas (GHG) and the collection
and flaring of the landfill gas would substantially reduce the GHG emissions from the site.
It is expected that energy recovery from the landfill gas would be economic as the site is
more extensively developed and in the long term could contribute of the order of several
megawatts to local electricity supplies. Moreover, its beneficial use would avoid the need
to dissipate very large amounts of thermal energy by means of a flare.
56.         Jinzhou Components. The development of new water resources for Jinzhou
would improve the quality of water in supply by virtue of substitution of sources that are
already contaminated or are at risk of contamination. The process improvements at the
Iincheng would have a major positive impact on water quality in the Daling River since
the mill wastewater represents by far the largest pollution load to the river. The process
improvements would reduce the pollution load by more than 2 million population
equivalent, largely as a result of the production and sale of the binder product produced



- 127 -                        ANNEX-8
from  the concentrated process liquor.  In addition, there would be substantial
improvements/savings in water (more than 60 percent) and process chemicals use and
product recovery.
Negative Environmental Impacts
57.         Although, as referred to above, the overall environmental impact of the
project is very substantially positive, there are nevertheless some negative impacts that
would require mitigation at the design and construction stages. In addition, the provision
of additional water resources for Jinzhou, although clearly beneficial in itself, would
neveadeless result in corresponding increases in wastewater quantities from Jinzhou, which
unless treated would adversely impact the appropriate receiving watercourses in the Daling/
Xiaoling Basin. The potential adverse impacts of LEP are listed in Table 4 and the
principal issues discussed below.
58.         Land Use. Significant areas of land would be necessary for the constuction
of the four wastewater treatment facilities and the water resource development at Jinzhou
as follows:
Anshan                  15 ha
Benxi                   22 ha
Dalian (Malan River)    5 ha
Fushun                  49 ha
Jinzhou                 5 ha
In addition, the Dalian landfill would be located within an area of 5 km2 previously used
for salt and prawn production.
59.         The site in Anshan is within an industrialized area and is currently unused.
Its use is therefore not considered to impose an adverse impact. The Benxi plant would
be located in an area that is already flood-prone. Thus, mitigation measures would be
necessary to protect the site from future flooding and adverse impacts are not therefore
significant. Only in the case of Fushun and Jinzhou would there be loss of agricultural
land, but the impact on the agricultural output of the region would not be significant.
Where temporary use of agricultural land is necessary for the construction of pipelines,
topsoil would be stored separately and the land reinstated. In the case of Dalian, the
construction of the plant would use land that could otherwise have been used for industry.
60.         Water AvailabilIty. The proposed Anshan wastewater treatment plant,
although improving very substantially the quality of any wastewater discharged from the
plant to the Xida Gou, would remove a significant quantity of water (220,000 m3kW) from
the clannel, which is a tributary of the Yunliang and ultimately the Taizi, both of which
are used for irrigation. However, the reuse of the treated wastewater would release the
coresponding amount of water from the municipal supply and the overall discharge of
wastewater to the catchment would remain the same.

61.         Resettlement. Only in the case of the Benxi treatment plant would there be
a need for any residential resettlement.  It is expected that 40-50 households
(approximately 200 people) would be relocated from an area contiguous to the proposed
treatment plant site to provide a sufficient sanitary buffer zone between the plant and the
nearest residence. Details of the resettlement arrangements are described in Annex 7.
62.        In the case of the Maoyingzi landfill site and the transfer station, the project
would take away the livelihood of the approximately 100 scavengers that remove recyclable
material from the waste stream (amounting to about 2 percent), thereby deriving an income
of some Y 2,000/month.
53.         Spoil Disposal. Spoil would be generated from construction of all facilities
involving excavations. Spoil would be used for construction fill where needed or for other
uses such as road construction and landscaping. Spoil in excess of local requirements
would be disposed of in accordance with an approved disposal plan.
64.         Residues Disposal. Sludges would be generated at the wastewater treatment
plants at Anshan, Benxi, Dalian and Fushun. 7ince industry generates a major proportion
of the wastewater flow, the sludges would likely contain significant quantities of pollutants
of industrial origin, such as heavy metals, and would not be suitable for reuse ir.
agriculre. Sludge disposal would in all cases by landfill in sites that are environmentally
secure and/or have suitable environmental controls. Proposals for sludge disposal for the
five cities are given in Table 5.
65.         A residue would also be generated by the electrostatic precipitators to be
illed at the blast furnaces in Benxi. It is expected that this solid residue would be
reused in cement production, but if this proves not to be feasible, disposal would be to a
suitably designed landfill.
66.         Construction Impacts. The principal adverse impacts of construction
activities are on urban air quality and noise levels. Increased dust from construction
activities would be temporary and effects can be mitigated by, for example, water sprays.
The effects of increased noise levels may be minimized by controls on hours of worldng.
Pipeline construction may cause temporary disruption to traffic and other services. Once
construction is complete, all roads would be reinstated and other areas regraded to allow
appropriate use such as agriculture.
