- 134 -                       AN1       11
LIAONG                OM                  (E
1.         China is taking a variety of measures to bring municipal and industrial
pollution under control. One method, addressed to industries, is to create revolving loan
funds at the provincial or municipal level that provide subsidized financing for the control
of liquid, solid and gaseous wastes, particularly to those can produce greater social and
environmental benefits. A regulatory framework wherein industries are required to neet
specified waste discharge standards and an institutional structure to organize ane kperate
the funds are prerequisite to their success.
2.         In 1982, Chinese environmental laws provided for the establishment of an
environment fund financed by pollution fees. These provided local-level (province,
municipality and county) subsidies and grants for pollution reduction investments in
industrial and municipal pollution reduction projects, and environmental monitoring and
enforcement for the EPBs. In 1988, an amendment allowed about 20-30 percent of the
fees to be provided to enterprises as a loan; some cities are still experimenting with this.
Among the provinces in China, Liaoning has the highest pollution fee collection amount
and the Shenyang Environmental Fund is considered a model of pollution revolving fund
for the country.
Pollution Fee Collection and Use in Liaoning Province
3.         In Liaoning, pollution fee collection is executed by the municipal and county
EPBs, while fee collection and uftlization planning are jointly drawn up by provincial,
municipal and county EPBs. According to fund allocation plan provided by the EPBs, the
local finance bureaus issue order and extend funds to subprovincial level PCBCs for loan
disbursement. Currently, about 950 persons are working in the pollution levy offices of the
EPBs in Liaoning.
4.          Fees are assessed according to waste discharge information provided to levy
offices by the local monitoring stations. On the average, large polluting industries would
be monitored monthly; however, due to lack of monitoring forces, some industries receive
their fee bill according to waste discharge load estimate by monitoring station. In
Liaoning, the top 100 polluters contribute to 75 percent of the total fees collected.
5.          Fee rates have been established for wastewater discharges, waste gas
emissions, solid waste dumping and noise pollution. Between 1980 to 1992, total fee
collection anounts to Y 1.41 billion. Of the collected fees, about 70 percent were used
for industrial pllution control, 10 percent for nonindustrial environmental improvement



- 135 -                       ANW        l1
projects and 20 percent for EPBs' environmental monitoring and enforcement. During
1986-90 period, about 6,616 industrial pollution control projects (48 of them with
investment over Y 1.0 million) were supported by pollution fee fund, totaled about Y 550
million, account for about 42 percent of the needed investment. Of the above, 3,217
projects have been completed, increased annual industrial wastewater treatment capacity
by 104 million cubic meters waste gas emission treatment by 70.6 billion standard cubic
meters and solid waste treatment by 2.8 million tons, corresponding to new treatment
capacities of 21.5 percent, 52.8 percent and 23.7 percent. Resource recovery projects
produced Y 175 million during the same period. Pollution fees for industrial pollution
control clearly played an important role in Liaoning. Fee collection efficiency for
Liaoning was about 70 percent in 1992. By the end of the 1991-96 period, the total fee
collection is expected to reach Y 250 million per year in Liaoning, due to new rates to be
enforced and strengthening of fee collection management.
6.          Bank Experience in China with Environmental Funds. The Bank has
supported the establishment of environmental funds under four different projects and three
of them have been in operation for at least one year. The Bank-assisted funds were found
to have the following superior features:
(a)   provided a stronger framework for management, including organization,
staffing and operation regulations, and, indirectly, providing the basis for
other environmental protection management measures including the permit
system and the promotion of pollution prevention programs;
(0)   instituted rigorous requirements and procedures for project preparation and
appraisal ensuring a higher project success rate; and
(c)   provided training for capacity-building to staff of the fund offices in the
technical and financial areas.
7.          On the f ier hand, because the great majority of the borrowers are small-
and medium-sized ente rises requiring loans under $1.0 million, the appraisal procedures
could be modified in th& future in order to be tailored to the circumstances.
The Liaoning Environment Fund (LEE)
8.          Objective. The purpose of establishing LEF is to strengthen the existing
Liaoning pollution prevention program with a technically, institutionally and financially
sustainable mechanism. The Fund would primarily assist industrial enterprises to control
pollution through waste minimization measures, modifications or renovations to existing
plants to reduce waste outputs or to recycle waste generated during production. Industrial
upgrading projects designed to reduce the amount of pollutant discharge and to save natural
resources and energy, commercial waste recovery services and centralized treatment plants
would also be considered by the Fund.



- 136 -                       AiNE..I1
9.          Organization and Financing of LEF. LEF is chartered by the Liaoning
Provincial Government (LPG) as an autonomous, nonprofit organization, with initial capital
equivalent of Y 2.0 million, registered with the Liaoning Bureau of Industry and
Commerce as an entity. The Bank Loan would provide $4.0 million and LEPB would
contribute from industrial pollution discharge fees (Y 2.0 million for each of the first two
years and Y 10.0 million per year thereafter).
10.        LPG would appoint a five-member Steering Committee comprised of
representatives from LEPB, the Commission of Planning and the Finance Bureau of
Liaoning. The Steering Committee would propose policies for application for LEF
funding, formulate rules and regulations for Fund management, select a depository agency
for the Fund and define the terms and conditions for Fund loans. The LEF Steering
Committee would also determine institutional structure and staff composition of the LEF
Management Office and approve its annual work plan and budget.
11.        The Fund Management Office (FMO) would be established to consist of
12 positions, to be filled during a three-year period, including specialists in environmental
science and technology, industral processing, economics and finance, and administradve
and support staff. The director would be appointed by the Steering Committee, and most
other staff would be locally recruited. The Director of FMO is the legal person of LEF.
The main role of FMO would be in investment project planning, coordination between
borrower and agent bank, review of project feasibility and supervision of project
implementation. A specialists' consortium would be formed to provide specific expertise
needed in project evaluation.
12.        Fund Management. Specific management procedures are prescribed in
LEE operational rules and procedures, including project selection criteria, project
management procedures and aspects of financial management.
13.        Project Selection. Each application would have to be reviewed by its local-
level industrial bureau and planning commission, and approved by the concerned local
Environmental Protection Bureau to ensure consistency with the municipal environmental
planning. Based on the general project selection criteria mentioned above, a formula for
ranldng has been developed to prioritize submitted project proposals.
Project Management Procedures
14.        LEF operating procedures have been drafted and would be approved by the
LEE Steering Committee. Fundamental project management procedures are:
(a)   The Fund Management Office would issue LEF directives and solicitations
for project proposals to the sublevel provincial environmental protecton
agencies and planning agencies;



- 137-                       ANNEX 11
(b) With consent from the local industrial bureau, the enterprise would submit
a loan application to the environmental protection agency and planning
agency of its location;
(c) The environmental protection agency and planning agency would review the
application according to Fund selection criteria and formula for project
prioritization;
(d)   The enterprise would prepare a feasibility study report, including a financial
proposal for investment and environmental impact assessment (EIA). FMO
would have to inform the Bank about the proposed projects for approval
before appraisal is to be carried by the agent bank.
(e)   After the project has been appraised by the agent bank, FMO would submit
the appraisal report to the World Bank for approval. The Bank would only
review and approve the first five subloan projects and thereafter each
subloan of over $300,000. Then FMO would then develop a loan plan
includi1ig identifying the loan extension period and loan period according to
the project type, construction period and economic benefits.
(f)   The LEF Steering Committee would be responsible for the final approval
of subloan projects. FMO would issue the loan plan to the local bureaus in
charge, the cofinancing agencies and the agent bank;
(g)   The project unit, upon receipt of the loan plan, would arrange for its
implementation.
(h)   The FMO would supervise the implementation of the project.
(i)   After a defined period of commissioning of the operation, the project unit
would submit an application for project examination and acceptance to the
bureaus in charge of the project. As proof of satisfactory completion of the
project, a Certificate of Examination and Acceptance would be issued to the
project unit, which would make inference to the environmental agency's
monitoring report;
(j)   The bureau in charge would submit examination and acceptance documents
for the project to FMO;
(k)  If, upon examination and acceptance after project completion, the project
still does not meet the design document requirements, FMO would arrange
for appropriate departments to develop amendments to the project.



- 138-                        ANNEX 11
Project Appraisal
15.        The China Investment Bank (CIB), Liaoning Branch, has been selected to
be the agent bank for LEF. Its responsibilities include contracting and supervising the
work of technical appraisal agent(s), undertaking financial appraisal, manage disbursement
and supervise expenditures. The appraisal would follow the CIB Appraisal Manual for use
on Bank-financed projects. CIB would contract agent(s) for technical appraisal and the
possible candidates are Liaoning Environmental Protection Engineering Consulting
Company and the industrial consulting firms affiliated to industrial bureaus and design
institutes. CIB would provide monthly project statements to FMO reporting on both the
LEF-financed portion and the project-financed portion. FMO would collect the principal
and the interest of the loan; the agent bank would provide any necessary assistance.
16.        For the technical appraisal of individual projects, the general criteria to be
considered are: (a) the impact to the ambient environment before and after the project,
(b) unit cost of investment per unit pollution load reduction, (c) efforts made on pollution
prevention, (d) compliance with environmental regulations and standards; and (e) whether
it is technical feasible and has produced the le:Lst-cost option.
17.        The economic appraisal for  vestment of the individual enterprise must
show the enterprise is economically viable, . indicated by the internal rate of return (IRR)
of the subproject.
18.        For the financial appraisal of the subproject, each enterprise would have to
show if it, as a whole, would be financially viable measured by debt service ratio, and this
value should be larger than 1.4. For subproject investing on joint waste treatment facility,
a financing plan for the operation and maintenance of the facility would be required,
including service charges made to the client enterprises.
Project Flnancing Procedures Between Agent Bank and Borrower
19.        CIB is the account-bearing bank as well as agent bank for LEF. Once a
subloan application is approved by LEF, CIB would execute financial management of the
loan according to procedures described below:
(a)   CIB would establish a financing plan of the loan with the project unit (the
borrower), in accordance with the loan agreement signed between LEF and
the enterprise.
(b)   The project unit wouid open an account with CIB and deposit its share of
the capital raised for the project.
(c)   CIB would disburse funds upon receipt of statement of expenditure, in the
form of invoice or letter of credit, to the project unit as reimbursement for
project expenses. Disbursement would be made once a month.



- 139 -                       ANNEX 11
(d)   CIB would supervise the fund's use by the project unit. If project funds are
found to have been used for any purpose other than the approved project,
CIB would refuse further disbursement and take measure for rectification.
(e)   CIB would report to LEF quarterly on the financial status of loans made to
borrowers; CIB would also report emerging issues and make suggestions for
improvement as needed.
(f)   At project completion CIB would finalize the financial accounting.
(g)   If projects fail to meet project date or design criteria, upon consultation with
the LEF, CIB would terminate disbursement.
(h)   CIB would assist LEF in the collection of loan principal, interest, late
payment penalties and fines.
20.         CIB Liaoning would assist in the collection of subloan repayments for
subproject, review of contract package prepared by FMO and the project entity, and
determine the procurement method of the various subprojects basically following the same
procedures as Bank-financed CIB projects.
21.         Disbursement would be made through CIB from the special account for LEP
in the Liaoning Finance Bureau. According to payment schedule prescribed in the
contract, and borrowers would submit a budget proposal to the agent Bank in advance of
any disbursements. Project entity would pay for project cost, then be reimbursed by CIB.
The final installment would not be paid until the project unit has received its waste
discharge permit from the local EPB. Fund project accounts would be audited annually,
as would other project components.
LemM
22.         The LEF loan for each project unit would be limited to 100 prcent of
foreign exchange costs, or 50 percent of total project costs (excluding land), whichever is
higher. LEF would contribute 50 percent maximum of the total project costs and furer
the project size would not exceed $1 million and the loan size for each project would not
exceed $400,000. The LEF would bear the subloans' credit risk. The Fund subloan
interest rate would be the IBRD standard variable rate plus a spread of 1.5 percent per
year and a commitment charge of 0.75 percent. The project unit would bear the foreign
exchange risk according to the Foreign Debt Risk Act of China. The Fund loan period
would be between three to five years. LEF loan grace periods would be determined by
project nature, construction time, loan repayment ability, as well as the expected
environmental benefits. Repayments to LEF would be recycled for additional similar
subprojects to the extent funds are not needed for repayment by LEF of its subordinate
loan.



-140 -                        ANNEX II
23.         Repayments and Default. In case of default, FMO is entitled to deduct the
outstanding part of the loan within a certain period of time, and is entitled to collect extra
interest as the overdue payment fine. FMO would also take other necessary measures to
protect its interest.
24.         Responsibilities of the Recipient. The loan recipient must not appropriate
the loan for any other purposes. Should the recipient do so, FMO would withdraw the
loan and grant with the grant interest as well as extra interest as the overdue repayment
fine.
25.         Liabritles. The loan recipient would be responsible for project losses
caused by project design, construction, fmance management, or any other unforeseen
factors.
LEF Project Pipeline
26.         A proposed subloan project pipeline has been prepared by LEPB (see Table
below). The prefeasibility of two of the proposed subloan projects have been reviewed:
(a) the detoxication of Cr(+6) slag and its utilization in making P 'oy roller ball in Jinzhou
Ferro-alloy plant, and (b) the recovery of combustible gas from electric arc furnace and
purification of waste air emission of Liaoyang Ferro-alloy plant. The two plants are now
proceeding with the preparation of their appraisal reports that would be appraised by CuB.
Istitutional Development and Equipment Needs
27.         The Fund Management Office personnel would undergo an extensive training
program. Training courses would include economic and financial analysis, waste
management, waste reduction technology particularly in resource recovery/recycling and
clean technology. Training and equipments for LEF are covered under Package C,
environmental quality management, monitoring and control.

- 146 -                       ANNEX  3
FIMANCIAL ANALYSIS ASSUMI  ONS
A. JINzHou WATER SUPPLY COMPANY
1.          Assumptions to the projections of the main financial statements of the
Jinzhou Water Supply Company (JWSC) for the period 1994-2001 are provided below.
2.          Inflation and Exchange Rates.  Yearly general domestic inflation rates
used in the projections are 12.0 percent for 1994, 9.0 percent in 1995, 8.0 percent in
1996, 7.2 percent in 1997, 6.5 percent in 1998-99 and 6.0 percent in 2000-01. Foreign
price increases are estimated at 2.8 percent for each of years 1994-2001. The exchange
rate used to convert foreign costs to local currency, where applicable, was Y 8.7 per $1.0.
It is assumed that exchange rate adjustments would, on average, maintain purchasing
power parity over the projection period.
Income Statement
3.          Water Sales. Projections of sales are based on "minimum demand" and
maximum  capacity figures.  Unaccounted-for-water is estimated at 11 percent of
production, rising to 15 percent from 1997. It is assumed that whenever demand exceeds
supply, the shortfall would be borne by both the domestic and nondomestic categories of
consumers, proportionally.
4.          Tariffs. The domestic tariff, in effect since July 1, 1993, is Y 0.50 per i3.
The capital construction and service industries (includes cold drinks industry) tariff, also
introduced from July 1, 1993, and which includes a water resources fee of Y 0.04 per n3,
is Y 1.54 per m3. The industrial tariff was raised on May 1, 1993 from Y 0.59 to Y 0.84
per me (which includes a water resource fee of Y 0.04 per m3. The net average prices per
m3 in current terms over the projected period are as follows: Y 0.79 in 1994; Y 1.06-
1995; Y 1.21-1996; Y 1.28-1997; Y 1.37-1998; Y 1.46-1999; Y 1.54-2000; and
Y 1.63-2001. The ratio between domestic tariffs and net nondomestic tariffs is about
35:65.
5.          Other Charges. Industries that exceed 90 percent of their previous year's
consumption (the base), would be subject to excess water charges per i3, as follows:
Y 1.24 between 1 and 10 percent over the base; Y 1.64 between 11 and 20 percent;
Y 2.04 between 21 and 30 percent; and Y 2.44 over 31 percent of the base. The above
charges include the water resource fee of Y 0.04 per m3. As it would be difficult to
estimate the quantum of "excess" water consumed, no assumptions of such charges have
been included in the projections.



- 147-                         ANNEX 13
6.          A one-time charge of Y 5.00 per m2 of construction area is applicable for
connecting new residential and office buildings to the water supply system. The
projections assume an annual construction of 150,000 m2 against which this charge would
apply.
7.          The above "excess water" and construction area charges, which accrue to
JWSC, became effective from July 1, 1993. The water resource fee of Y 0.04 per m3 is
paid to the Water Conservancy Bureau.
8.          Operating Costs. Salaries and wages are assumed to increase at the rates
given in para. 2 above. Energy prices are assumed to increase in line with general
inflation. Materials and other costs are assumed to increase at the general inflation rate.
Depreciation for plant and machinery is taken at 7 percent. For other fixed assets,
depreciation is taken at 3.9 percent of gross fixed assets in operation. Sales tax, including
an urban construction surtax and an education surtax, is at 3.27 percent of gross operating
revenue; and a provincial profits tax is at 33 percent of net income.
9.          Interest and Amortization Expenses. The proceeds of the IBRD loan are
assumed to be onlent by Jinzhou Municipal Government (JMG) to JWSC at the IBRD's
standard variable interest rate (which was 7.27 percent per year at the time of
negotiations), and 0.75 percent per year commitment charge, over 15 years, including
5 years of grace. Interest is paid annually. Amortization of loans would be on the basis
of equal payments of principal. JWSC would bear the foreign exchange risk. Other loans
from JMG are at about 11.5 percent per year over three to five years with equal
repayments of principal starting on completion of the disbursement period.
Balance Sheet
10.         Inventories. Inventories have been projected to take into account general
inflation as well as any expanded levels of operations and construction.
11.         Accounts Receivable. Accounts receivable from water sales are assumed
to be 120 percent of monthly revenue in 1994, or about 36 days' revenue.
12.         Fixed Assets. JWSC's fixed assets are valued at historic costs. As a state-
owned enterprise, JWSC is not permitted to revalue its assets. In the projections,
construction work-in-progress is assumed to be 100 percent accounted for upon completion.
Source and Application of Funds
13.         Working Capital Needs. Working capital needs represent the excess, or
otherwise, of the current year's current assets (net of cash), less the excess of the previous
year's current assets (net of cash) over current liabilities.
14.         Change In Cash. Change in cash (which includes short-term investments)
calculates the balance sheet cash balance for the current year.



- 148 -                       ANNEX 13
B. WASTEWATER COI4ANIES
15.        Assumptions to the projections of the main financial statements of the
Anshan, Benxi, Dalian and Fushun Wastewater Companies for the period 1994-2001 are
provided below.
16.        Inflation and Exchange Rates. Yearly general domestic inflation rates used
in the projections are 12.0 percent for 1994, 9.0 percent in 1995, 8.0 percent in 1996,
7.2 percent in 1997, 6.5 percent in 1998-99 and 6.0 percent in 2000-02. Foreign price
increase are estimated at 2.8 percent for each of years 1994-2001. The exchange rate
used to convert foreign costs to local currency, where applicable, was Y 8.7 per $1.0. It
is assumed that exchange rate adjustments would, on average, maintain purchasing power
parity over the projection period.
Income Statement
17.        Sales. Projections of sewerage quantities are based on "minimum demand"
and maximum capacity figures, and at the equivalent of 80 percent of water bills.
18.        Average Tariffs. The average prices in Yuan per m3 in current terms are
as follows:
1224  122}  19261927 i2M  1222  ; 2sQ  2g

Fushun      0.42  0.46  0.62  0.67  0.71  0.78  0.83  0.88
19.        The above average tariffs are assumed to increase in steps up to the year
1996 to cover the projected costs of treatment on the project-financed treatment plants due
to enter service around 1998, as well as the collection and disposal costs of wastewater.
This was done to minimuie the need for substantial increases in the tariffs to cover
treatment costs when the plants enter service. From 1997, the tariffs increase generally
with inflation.
20.         Treat d Wastewater Sales. Anshan and Dalian Wastewater Companies
anticipate selling a part of, or all, their treated wastewater production to industry. The
projected tariffs per m3 are shown below. The projections assume Anshan would sell all
its treated wastewater; Dalian would sell 50 percent of its treated wastewater.

21.         Operating Costs. Salaries, wages and staff benefits are assumed to increase
at the rates given in para. 16 above. Energy, materials and other costs are assumed to
increase in line with general inflation also. Depreciation for plant and machinery is taken
at 6.0 percent. For other fixed assets, depreciation is taken at between 3.3 and 4 percent
of gross fixed assets in operation. Business tax is 3.27 percent, which includes an urban
construction surtax and an education surtax. Provincial income tax is 33 percent of net
income.
22.         Interest and Amortization Expenses. The proceeds of the IBRD loan are
assumed to be onlent to the Anshan, Benxi, Dalian and Fushun Wastewater Companies by
their respective Municipal Govemments at the IBRD's standard variable interest rate
(which was 7.27 percent per year at the time of negotiations), and 0.75 percent per year
commitment charge over 15 years, including 5 years of grace. Interest is paid annually.
Amordzation of loans would be on the basis of equal payments of principal. The
wastewater companies would bear the foreign exchange risk. The municipalities would
provide the local capital counterpart funds as capital grants.
Balance Sheet
23.         Inventories. Inventories have been projected to take into account general
inflation as well as any expanded levels of operations and construction.
24.         Accounts Receivable. Accounts receivable are assumed to be 49 percent
of monthly billings, or about 15 days' revenue.
Source and Application of Funds
25.         Working Capital Needs. Working capital needs represent the excess, or
otherwise, of the current year's current assets (net of cash), less the excess of the previous
year's current assets (net of cash) over curent liabilities.
26.         Change in Cash. Change in cash (which includes short-term investments)
calculates the balance sheet cash balance for the current year.

D. DALIAN SoLID WASTE COMPANY

38.         Inflation and Exchange Rates. Yearly general domestic inflation rates used
in the projections are 12.0 percent for 1994, 9.0 percent in 1995, 8.0 percent in 1996,
7.2 percent in 1997, 6.5 percent in 1998-99, and 6.0 percent in 2000-2001. Foreign price
increases are estimated at 2.8 percent for each of years 1994-2001. The exchange rate
used to convert foreign costs to local currency, where applicable, was Y 8.7 per $1.0. It
is assumed that exchange rate adjustments would, on average, maintain purchasing power
parity over the projection period.
Income Statement
39.         Revenue. Revenues are based on projections of solid wastes to be disposed
of at the landfill, as follows: (a) 100 percent of the residential and institutional wastes
generated in Dalian; (b) the maximum permissible wastes allowable from the industrial
sector of 93,600 tons annually; and (c) 100 percent of the annual sludge waste.
40.         Tariffs. The prices in Yuan per ton in current terms are as follows:

landfill tipping fee. Industrial wastes are not allowed to be routed through the transfer
station. Industries are therefore required to make their own arrangements for disposal of
their nontoxic, nonhazardous wastes at the landfill, and would be charged the landfill
tipping fee only.
42.         Operating Costs. Salaries, wages and staff benefits are assumed to increase
at the rates given in para. 38 above. Energy, materials and other costs are assumed to
increase in line with general inflation also. Depreciation for plant and machinery is taken
at about 11.9 percent. For other fixed assets, depreciation is taken at about 3.8 percent
of gross fixed assets in operation. Land tax is Y 1.50 per m2 for the transfer station,
Y 1.20 per m2 for the landfill site. Building Tax is 70 percent of fixed assets multiplied
by 1.2 percent. Equipment Tax is Y 60.00 per tonnage of capacity of truck. Business tax
is 3.27 percent, which includes an urban construction surtax and an education surtax.
Income tax is 33 percent of net income.
